Allah's Existence
advanced
6 min
Razi's Dilemma: Imkan Cannot Be an Attribute of Essence or Existence
Second half of Razi's third proof: imkan cannot belong to essence or existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that even if one accepts the non-existent as a thing, possibility (imkan) cannot be an attribute of either the unchangeable essence or of non-existent existence.

Core Idea
Imkan cannot stick to the immutable essence or non-existent existence.

In the second part of his third proof, Razi turns the argument against those who concede that the non-existent is a thing. He presents a dilemma: possibility must be an attribute (sifa) of either the essence (mahiyya) or existence. Both alternatives are impossible, as he will show.

Guided Path
1
Read the full dilemma
Read the Arabic section from 'وأيضا' to the end. Note the two possibilities: imkan as attribute of mahiyya or of existence.
Razi uses the term 'الماهية' (essence) and 'الوجود' (existence).
2
Understand the first impossibility
Razi argues that imkan cannot be an attribute of the essence because the essence cannot change or be described with temporal attributes. Essences are immutable by definition.
Key phrase: 'لأن الماهية يستحيل عليها الانقلاب والتغير'.
3
Understand the second impossibility
Imkan cannot be an attribute of existence because existence before its occurrence is not established (laysa thabitan). But imkan is posited before existence (qabl al-huduth). So an attribute cannot inhere in something that does not yet exist.
Razi points out that imkan is established before existence, but existence itself is not.
4
Conclude the argument
Since neither option works, imkan itself is incoherent. This completes Razi's third proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة: أنا إذا قلنا الشيء يجوز أن يكون موجودا، ويجوز أن يكون معدوما يقتضي تقرر ذلك الشيء حال وصفه بكونه معدوما، وهذا يقتضي كون المعدوم شيئًا، وأنتم لا تقولون به. وأيضا : القائل بأن المعدوم شيء لا يمكنه القول بالإمكان؛ وذلك لأن الإمكان على هذا التقدير إما أن يكون وصفًا للماهية أو وصفًا للوجود ولا جائز أن يكون وصفًا للماهية ؛ لأن الماهية يستحيل عليها الانقلاب والتغير، فلا يعقل كون الإمكان وصفًا لها، ولا جائز أن يكون وصفًا للوجود لأن الوجود قبل تجدده وحدوثه ما كان ثابتا ولا متعينا والإمكان عندكم ثابت قبل الحدوث، وإذا كان كذلك امتنع القول بجعل الإمكان صفة للوجود.
The third proof: When we say that something can be existent and can be non-existent, this necessitates that thing being determined while described as non-existent, and this necessitates that the non-existent is a thing, and you (opponents) do not hold that. Also, whoever says that the non-existent is a thing cannot hold possibility (al-imkan), because possibility on this account is either an attribute of the essence (mahiyya) or an attribute of existence. It cannot be an attribute of the essence because the essence cannot undergo change and alteration, so it is not conceivable that possibility be an attribute of it. And it cannot be an attribute of existence because existence before its renewal and coming-to-be was not established nor determined, while possibility in your view is established before coming-to-be. Since this is so, the statement that possibility is an attribute of existence is precluded.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a third proof against imkan. Razi argues that saying something is possible requires the thing to be determined even when non-existent, implying the non-existent is a thing – which opponents deny. He then turns to those who accept the non-existent is a thing: they still cannot hold imkan because it would be an attribute of either the essence (mahiyya) or existence. Essences are immutable, so imkan cannot be an attribute of them. Existence does not exist before it comes to be, while imkan is posited before existence. Thus imkan is impossible.

Key Terms
ماهية
وجود
انقلاب
تغير
حدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Possibility can be an attribute of the essence because essences are eternal and can be described with possibilities.
Correction: Razi argues that essences are immutable (لا يستحيل عليها الانقلاب والتغير), so they cannot be described with an attribute like possibility, which implies potential for change.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, why can possibility (imkan) not be an attribute of the essence (mahiyya)?
A) Because essences are non-existent.
B) Because essences are eternal and cannot be described.
C) Because the essence does not undergo change or alteration.
D) Because possibility is an attribute of existence only.

Key Takeaway
Razi closes his argument by showing that even accepting the non-existent as a thing, imkan cannot be attributed to the immutable essence or pre-existent existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own potential—your hopes, your capabilities—do you treat them as permanent attributes of who you are? Razi argues that possibility (imkan) cannot be an attribute of the immutable essence. How does this confront the way you define yourself by your potential? Will you reassign your sense of worth from what you might become to what God has already established in His knowledge?
?
Razi says that existence, before it comes to be, is not established. That means you have not always existed and your existence is a fresh act of creation each moment. Does this awareness break your illusion of self-sufficiency? How can you cultivate a constant sense of gratitude for your existence as a gift rather than an inherent right?
?
If imkan cannot be an attribute of either essence or existence, then what can you truly claim as your own? Razi's argument strips away any false sense of independence. What are you going to do today to remind yourself that your very possibility to do anything is not a property of your nature but a direct creation of Allah?

Redefining Imkan: Continuity and Cessation
Razi redefines imkan and addresses a remaining objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi redefines imkan to resolve earlier doubts and why a further objection forces a return to the first proof.

Core Idea
Imkan is not a real attribute but the possibility of continuing or ceasing.

Razi now clarifies that by 'imkan' he does not mean a real attribute but simply that something can either continue as it is or not. This defuses the earlier objections. However, a subtle objection remains: why could the originator of bodies not be itself originated but possible? Razi acknowledges this and points to the first proof for the final answer. This lesson traces the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let Razi's own wording come through before you interpret.
Notice the structure: a definition then its application.
2
Identify Razi's definition of imkan
Find where Razi says 'our intention from possibility is...' and understand that it means something can either continue or cease. This is the key move.
Compare with the earlier definition of imkan as 'neither necessary nor impossible'.
3
Understand the remaining objection and the redirection
Razi ends by acknowledging a possible objection: why could the One who originated bodies not have been originated itself, but be possible? He says to answer this we must return to the first proof. Think about why this objection is serious and how the first proof resolves it.
This shows that the redefinition alone is not enough; a deeper proof is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب : مرادنا من الإمكان هو كون الشيء بحيث يجوز أن يستمر على ما كان عليه قبل ذلك، ويجوز أن لا يبقى على ما كان عليه قبل ذلك، وإذا ظهر مرادنا من لفظ الإمكان زالت الشبهات المذكورة. وإذا عرفت هذا فنقول : بقاؤه على ما كان عليه قبل ذلك غير ممتنع وعدم بقائه أيضًا على ما كان عليه قبل ذلك غير ممتنع أيضاً، ولما جاز الأمران امتنع رجحان أحدهما على الآخر، إلا لمرجح ، إلا أنه يبقى عليه أن يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يكون محدث الأجسام محدثًا، وإن كان قديمًا ولكنه جائز الوجود لذاته، إلا أن الوجود كان به أولي ؟ وعند هذا نفتقر في بيان كونه تعالى واجب الوجود لذاته إلى الرجوع إلى ما ذكرناه في البرهان الأول.
The response: Our intention from possibility (al-imkan) is that the thing is such that it may continue as it was before, and it may not remain as it was before. When our intention from the word imkan becomes clear, the aforementioned doubts disappear. And when you understand this, we say: its remaining as it was before is not impossible, and its not remaining as it was before is also not impossible. Since both are possible, one cannot be preferred over the other except by a preponderator. However, there remains to be said: why may it not be that the Originator of bodies is originated, although He is pre-eternal but possible of existence in His essence, except that existence would be more proper to Him? And at this point, in order to prove that He—may He be exalted—is necessary of existence in His essence, we need to return to what we mentioned in the first proof.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a response (al-jawab) to the earlier arguments against imkan. Razi clarifies what he means by imkan: not a real attribute, but simply that something can continue or cease. Once understood, the earlier confusions vanish. He then applies this to bodies: their remaining or ceasing is equally possible, so a preponderator is needed. But then an objection arises: why cannot the originator of bodies be itself originated, even if pre-eternal, but possible? Razi acknowledges that this objection forces one to go back to the first proof (al-burhan al-awwal) to establish that God is necessary of existence in His essence. So this response is not the final answer but a redirection.

Key Terms
إمكان
استمرار
بقاء
مرجح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Razi has fully resolved the issue with his redefinition of imkan.
Correction: Razi himself acknowledges a further objection that cannot be answered by the redefinition alone; it requires the first proof to establish God's necessity.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's response, what is the meaning of imkan (possibility) that removes the earlier doubts?
A) That something may be either existent or non-existent in itself
B) That something may continue as it was or not continue
C) That something has a potential to exist
D) That something is neither necessary nor impossible

Key Takeaway
Razi's redefinition of imkan as the possibility of continuing or ceasing clears earlier objections, but a further objection shows the need for a more fundamental proof of God's necessity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every contingent moment of your existence requires a Preponderator to tilt the scales toward continuation, are you living with the awareness that you are sustained from one breath to the next by Allah's will?
?
Razi admits his redefinition is not enough—he must return to a more fundamental proof. What is the foundational proof that grounds your own certainty in Allah? Have you ever truly wrestled with it, or do you avoid the depth?
?
The objection suggests that even the Originator might be possible in essence. Have you ever entertained a diluted concept of God's necessity? How does Razi's insistence on absolute, essence-based necessity confront the casual way you might speak or think about Allah?

The Intuitive Proof: Self-Evident Need for an Originator
Razi presents the common ground and the intuitive method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi presents the intuitive (daruri) proof that originated things need an originator, and why it is considered self-evident.

Core Idea
The need for a Creator is as obvious as a building needing a builder.

Razi begins by stating the common ground: bodies are originated and need an originator. He then introduces the first of two methods among mutakallimun: those who hold that this need is known intuitively. This lesson explores their argument and the example of a building, which shows the premise is self-evident.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the common ground
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Observe that Razi first establishes the shared foundation: bodies are originated (muhdath) and every originated thing needs an originator (muhdith).
He deliberately avoids discussing whether the originator is possible or necessary at this stage.
2
Identify the first method and its claim
The first group of mutakallimun claim that knowledge of this need is necessary (daruri) and self-evident (badihi). Understand what this means.
3
Analyze the building example
Razi gives the example of seeing a high building or well-constructed palace. Why does he say denial of a builder is judged as insanity? What does this reveal about human nature?
This example is meant to show that the premise is universally compelling.
4
Connect to the conclusion
From the example, Razi concludes that the premise 'every originated thing needs an originator' is self-evident. How does he justify this leap?
The compulsion to infer a maker from a made thing is innate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثالثة. الطريق الثاني في تقرير هذا البرهان أن نقول : الأجسام محدثة، وكل محدث فهو محتاج إلى المحدث من غير تعرض لكون ذلك المحدث جائزًا أو واجبًا - وأكثر مشايخ المتكلمين كانوا معولين على هذه الطريقة - ثم لهؤلاء طريقان : الأول : الذين قالوا : العلم باجتماع المحدث إلى المؤثر علم ضروري قالوا : والذي يدل عليه أن كل من رأى بناء رفيعا وقصرًا مشيدًا اضطر إلى العلم بأن له بانيا صانعاً، حتى إن من جوز حدوث ذلك البناء لا عن فاعل كان محكوما عليه بالجنون، فعلمنا أن هذه المقدمة بديهية . الثاني: الذين قالوا بأن هذه المقدمة استدلالية - وهم أكثر شيوخ المعتزلة كـ" أبو علي " و " هاشم" - وطريقهم هو أنهم يثبتون كون العبد موجدا لأفعال نفسه، يثبتون أن أفعالنا إنما افتقرت إلينا لأنها حدثت بعد أن كانت معدومة، وعند هذا يظهر أن الحدوث علة للافتقار إلى المحدث، فالعالم لما كان محدثًا الفاعل، وعلى تمسكهم بهذا القياس سؤالات صعبة :
The third issue. The second way in establishing this proof is to say: Bodies are originated, and every originated thing is in need of an originator, without addressing whether that originator is possible or necessary—and most of the leading scholars of the mutakallimun relied upon this way. Then these (scholars) have two methods: The first: those who said that knowledge of the originated thing's need for an effecter is necessary knowledge. They said: what indicates that is that everyone who sees a high building and a well-constructed palace is compelled to know that it has a builder and maker, to the point that one who allows that this building originated without a maker is judged to be insane. Thus we know that this premise is self-evident. The second: those who said that this premise is inferential—and they are most of the leading Mu'tazila, like Abu Ali and Hashim. Their method is that they establish that the servant is an originator of his own actions; they establish that our actions are in need of us because they occurred after being non-existent. From this it becomes clear that origination is the cause of need for an originator. So the world, since it is originated, [needs] the agent. And upon their adherence to this analogy, there are difficult questions.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage introduces the second approach to proving the Creator. Razi states the common ground: bodies are originated, needing an originator. Most mutakallimun rely on this. He then divides them into two groups. The first holds that the need is intuitive (daruri) knowledge, exemplified by seeing a building and immediately knowing it had a builder; denial is insanity, so the premise is self-evident (badihi). The second group, mostly Mu'tazila like Abu Ali al-Jubba'i and Hashim, holds that the premise is inferential (istidlali). Their method: first establish that humans originate their own actions; our actions need us because they occur after non-existence. Thus origination (huduth) is the cause of need. By analogy, the world's origination implies need for an agent. Razi notes that this analogy faces difficult questions, which he will present next.

Key Terms
محدث
مؤثر
علم ضروري
بديهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the intuitive proof is irrational or merely subjective.
Correction: Razi shows it is based on a universal human compulsion, so much so that denial is considered insanity, making it a rational and objective premise.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, what example do the supporters of the intuitive method give to show that the need for an originator is self-evident?
A) A child knowing its parents
B) Seeing a high building or well-constructed palace
C) The rising of the sun each morning
D) The movement of the stars

Key Takeaway
The intuitive proof grounds the need for a Creator in a self-evident premise recognized by all rational people.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as though the need for a Creator is as obvious as a building needing a builder? If you truly believed this, what would you have to change about your daily priorities and sense of accountability?
?
When you look at the universe around you, do you feel the same immediate compulsion to acknowledge its Maker as you would when seeing a magnificent palace? If not, what distractions or assumptions are dulling that intuitive recognition in your heart?
?
The passage says that denying an originator for the building would be considered insanity. In what subtle ways do you deny your own need for an Originator by living as if you are self-sufficient? What specific act of reliance or gratitude will you commit to today to affirm that need?

The Inferential Proof: Analogical Reasoning from Human Actions
Razi describes the inferential method of the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the inferential (istidlali) method used by the Mu'tazila to prove the need for an originator through analogical reasoning from human actions.

Core Idea
Human actions prove that origination causes need; the world, being originated, likewise needs an originator.

Razi now turns to the second group of mutakallimun, mainly the Mu'tazila, who argue that the need for an originator is not intuitive but inferential. They first establish that humans originate their own actions, then reason by analogy that the world's origination implies a Creator. This lesson unpacks their argument and notes that it faces difficult questions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the second method
Read the Arabic and translation. Identify the two groups mentioned: the inferentialists are mostly Mu'tazila like Abu Ali and Hashim.
2
Understand the two-step argument
First, they prove that humans are the originators of their own actions. Second, they generalize the principle that origination (huduth) causes need for an originator.
The phrase 'حدثت بعد أن كانت معدومة' indicates that actions come into existence after non-existence.
3
Trace the analogy to the world
The world, being originated, must then have an originator by the same principle. How does this analogy work?
The Arabic has a slight textual issue: 'فالعالم لما كان محدثًا الفاعل' likely means 'the world, since it is originated, needs the agent'.
4
Note the difficult questions
Razi ends by saying this analogy faces difficult objections. This sets up the next part of his discussion.
These objections are not discussed here, but be aware that the inferential method is contested.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثالثة. الطريق الثاني في تقرير هذا البرهان أن نقول : الأجسام محدثة، وكل محدث فهو محتاج إلى المحدث من غير تعرض لكون ذلك المحدث جائزًا أو واجبًا - وأكثر مشايخ المتكلمين كانوا معولين على هذه الطريقة - ثم لهؤلاء طريقان : الأول : الذين قالوا : العلم باجتماع المحدث إلى المؤثر علم ضروري قالوا : والذي يدل عليه أن كل من رأى بناء رفيعا وقصرًا مشيدًا اضطر إلى العلم بأن له بانيا صانعاً، حتى إن من جوز حدوث ذلك البناء لا عن فاعل كان محكوما عليه بالجنون، فعلمنا أن هذه المقدمة بديهية . الثاني: الذين قالوا بأن هذه المقدمة استدلالية - وهم أكثر شيوخ المعتزلة كـ" أبو علي " و " هاشم" - وطريقهم هو أنهم يثبتون كون العبد موجدا لأفعال نفسه، يثبتون أن أفعالنا إنما افتقرت إلينا لأنها حدثت بعد أن كانت معدومة، وعند هذا يظهر أن الحدوث علة للافتقار إلى المحدث، فالعالم لما كان محدثًا الفاعل، وعلى تمسكهم بهذا القياس سؤالات صعبة :
The third issue. The second way in establishing this proof is to say: Bodies are originated, and every originated thing is in need of an originator, without addressing whether that originator is possible or necessary—and most of the leading scholars of the mutakallimun relied upon this way. Then these (scholars) have two methods: The first: those who said that knowledge of the originated thing's need for an effecter is necessary knowledge. They said: what indicates that is that everyone who sees a high building and a well-constructed palace is compelled to know that it has a builder and maker, to the point that one who allows that this building originated without a maker is judged to be insane. Thus we know that this premise is self-evident. The second: those who said that this premise is inferential—and they are most of the leading Mu'tazila, like Abu Ali and Hashim. Their method is that they establish that the servant is an originator of his own actions; they establish that our actions are in need of us because they occurred after being non-existent. From this it becomes clear that origination is the cause of need for an originator. So the world, since it is originated, [needs] the agent. And upon their adherence to this analogy, there are difficult questions.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage introduces the second approach to proving the Creator. Razi states the common ground: bodies are originated, needing an originator. Most mutakallimun rely on this. He then divides them into two groups. The first holds that the need is intuitive (daruri) knowledge, exemplified by seeing a building and immediately knowing it had a builder; denial is insanity, so the premise is self-evident (badihi). The second group, mostly Mu'tazila like Abu Ali al-Jubba'i and Hashim, holds that the premise is inferential (istidlali). Their method: first establish that humans originate their own actions; our actions need us because they occur after non-existence. Thus origination (huduth) is the cause of need. By analogy, the world's origination implies need for an agent. Razi notes that this analogy faces difficult questions, which he will present next.

Key Terms
استدلالي
قياس
محدث
مؤثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the inferential method is unproblematic and universally accepted.
Correction: Razi indicates that this analogy faces difficult questions, showing it is a contested proof.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, what do the Mu'tazila first establish before applying the analogy to the world?
A) That God is necessary
B) That humans are the originators of their own actions
C) That the world is eternal
D) That the intuitive proof is false

Key Takeaway
The inferential proof argues from human agency to divine agency through the common principle that origination necessitates an originator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If this inferential proof for God’s existence were to have a serious logical flaw, would your belief in God be shaken? Why or why not? Examine the foundation of your faith.
?
The Muʿtazila argued that your actions prove that origination requires an originator. In your daily life, do you truly sense your dependence on God in every action, or do you feel like the sole originator of your deeds? Be honest.
?
How comfortable are you with using rational arguments to defend your faith? Does relying on proofs like this give you certainty, or do you feel a gap between logical conclusions and heartfelt conviction? Commit to one specific step to strengthen both your reason and your heart.

Three Difficult Questions on the Inferential Proof
Razi lists three objections to the Mu'tazilite inferential proof for the need of an originator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three difficult questions that Imam Razi raises against the Mu'tazilite inferential proof for the need of an originator.

Core Idea
Three objections dismantle the inferential proof by attacking its core premises.

Imam Razi presents three penetrating objections to the Mu'tazilite argument that the world's contingency implies an originator. These objections challenge the very possibility of the proof, showing its reliance on contested assumptions about human agency, the nature of origination, and the specificity of causation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Razi enumerates three distinct su'alat (questions/objections).
2
Understand the first objection
The first objection denies that humans originate their own actions and suggests actions might happen by coincidence. Razi argues that if coincidental origination is impossible, apply that directly to the world, bypassing the analogy.
This objection targets the premise that humans are agents.
3
Grasp the second objection
Even if we grant human origination, Razi argues that origination (huduth) is not the cause of need for an agent. He claims to have already proven this.
This attacks the causal link between huduth and need.
4
Examine the third objection
Even if huduth is a cause, it might be a specific huduth conditioned by relation to particular actions. The world's huduth lacks that condition, so the analogy fails.
This is a subtle point about the specificity of causation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أولها : أنا لا نسلم أن الواحد منا مُحْدِثٌ لأفعال نفسه، وسيأتي تقريره إن شاء الله تعالى في مسألة خلق الأفعال، ولم لا يجوز أن يقال: إن أفعالنا تحدث عند قصودنا ودواعينا لا بقدرتنا وداعيتنا، بل على سبيل الاتفاق من غير مؤثر ؟ فإن قالوا : الحدوث على سبيل الاتفاق محال فليذكروا ذلك ابتداء في حدوث العالم حتى يدل حدوث العالم على وجود الفاعل من غير حاجة إلى ذكر هذا القياس. وثانيهما هب أن أفعالنا واقعة بقدرتنا ولكن لا نسلم أن علة الحاجة هي الحدوث، ودليله الوجوه الكثيرة التي قدمناها في أن الحدوث لا يمكن أن يكون علة للحاجة، ولا جزءًا لهذه العلة ولا شرطا لها . ثالثها هب أن حدوثها علة لحاجتها إلينا لكن لم لا يجوز أن تكون العلة ذلك الحدوث، أعني : ماهية الحدوث بشرط إضافتها إلى تلك الأفعال الخاصة - والعالم وإن حصل فيه الحدوث لكن لم يحصل فيه ذلك الشرط الخاص، فلا يلزم أن يحصل فيه الحاجة إلى الفاعل.
The first of them: We do not concede that any one of us is an originator of his own actions, and its confirmation will come, God willing, in the issue of the creation of actions. And why may it not be said that our actions occur upon our intentions and motives, not by our power and motive, but rather by way of coincidence without any effecter? If they say: 'Origination by way of coincidence is impossible,' let them mention that initially regarding the origination of the world, so that the origination of the world indicates the existence of the agent without need for this analogy. The second of them: Grant that our actions occur by our power, but we do not concede that the cause of need is origination (huduth). Its proof is the many considerations we have presented that origination cannot be the cause of need, nor a part of this cause, nor a condition of it. The third of them: Grant that their origination is the cause of their need for us, but why may it not be that the cause is that specific origination, meaning the essence of origination conditioned by its addition to those specific actions—and the world, although origination occurs in it, does not have that specific condition, so it does not necessitate that need for an agent occurs in it.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage lists three difficult questions (su'alat sa'ba) directed at the Mu'tazilite inferential proof. First objection: The very claim that humans originate their own actions is disputed; Razi will discuss this later in the issue of 'creation of actions' (khalq al-af'al). Moreover, it is possible that our actions happen coincidentally with our intentions, not caused by our power. If the opponent says coincidental origination is impossible, they should invoke that principle directly for the world, bypassing the need for analogy. Second objection: Even if we grant human origination, we do not grant that origination (huduth) is the cause of need. Razi claims to have already shown that huduth cannot be the cause, part, or condition of need. Third objection: Even if huduth is the cause for actions, it might be the specific huduth conditioned by relation to those particular actions. The world's huduth lacks that specific condition, so the analogy fails.

Key Terms
خلق الأفعال
القود
دواعي
اتفاق
علة الحاجة
ماهية الحدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the inferential proof is straightforward and impervious to objection.
Correction: Razi shows the proof depends on many contested premises regarding human agency, the nature of origination, and the specificity of causation.

Checkpoint
What is the first difficult question (su'al) against the Mu'tazilite inferential proof?
A) The world's origination is not proven
B) We do not concede that humans originate their own actions, and actions may happen by coincidence
C) The existence of God is self-evident
D) The Mu'tazila are not reliable

Key Takeaway
The inferential proof for an originator is vulnerable to multiple objections that question its foundational premises about agency, causation, and specificity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe that Allah is the Creator of all things, but do you truly accept that your own actions are also created by Him? When you sin, do you blame your circumstances or admit that your will is subordinate to Allah's decree? Reflect on the first objection: if actions occur without your full control, how does that shift your responsibility before Allah? Will you now consider your own agency as a gift from Him rather than independent power?
?
The Mu'tazila tried to prove Allah by analogy with human acts. Razi shows the flaw in that analogy. Where in your own life have you tried to understand Allah by comparing Him to yourself? Is it not easier to let the Qur'an and Sunnah define His attributes without your own projection? What assumption about Allah have you held that you now see is built on a false analogy? Repent of that and resolve to learn His names from revelation alone.
?
Razi's objections strip away false confidence in intellectual proofs. Are you building your faith on unquestioned assumptions? Which premise about Allah's existence have you never seriously examined? This lesson calls you to examine the foundations of your belief—not to doubt, but to know why you believe. Will you take time to list the premises you accept about Allah and test them against revelation and sound reason? Or will you continue relying on borrowed certainty?

Proof from Internal Signs: Creation from a Drop
Razi argues from human creation from a drop to a wise Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the creation of man from a sperm-drop to argue for a wise Creator, and why natural causes alone are insufficient.

Core Idea
A uniform drop cannot produce a diverse body by nature alone; a wise Maker is needed.

Razi now turns to the internal signs of creation, focusing on the human origin from a drop of fluid. This argument is deeply rooted in Qur'anic verses that invite reflection on human creation. By examining the physical formation of the body, Razi shows that the intricate diversity of organs and their consistent arrangement cannot be explained by blind natural processes or celestial forces. The passage presents a rigorous logical refutation of naturalist explanations, leading to the necessity of a purposeful Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through to get the flow of Razi's argument, then read the English translation carefully.
The passage is incomplete; the conclusion is missing, but the main reasoning is present.
2
Understand the two scenarios
Identify the two possibilities Razi considers: either the drop is homogeneous in reality or heterogeneous. Notice how he refutes both.
The first scenario imagines the drop as truly uniform; the second as apparently uniform but actually diverse.
3
Follow the logical consequences
For each scenario, trace why natural forces would produce a uniform shape (sphere) or a disordered arrangement. See how reality contradicts these outcomes.
Razi uses examples from philosophy and medicine to strengthen his argument.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Even though the text is cut off, the conclusion is clear: the body's order proves a wise Maker with power and choice.
The final sentence begins 'therefore we know that...' implying the existence of a Creator.

في القرآن العظيم في آيات كثيرة، وتقريرها أن نقول : النطفة جسم متشابه الأجزاء في الصورة والشكل فإما أن يقال: إنها متشابهة الأجزاء في الحقيقة أو ليست كذلك، وذلك لأن الأطباء يقولون : إن عند استيلاء حرارة الأجزاء في الطبيعة. فنقول : إن كل مركب لا بد وأن يكون مركبًا من أجزاء كل واحد منها يكون بسيطا في نفس الأمر وفي الحقيقة، وإذا كان كذلك فكل واحد من تلك الأجزاء يكون قابلا متشابه الأجزاء في الحقيقة، وتكون للقوة الطبيعية الفاعلة فيها قوة واحدة، ومتى كان الأمر كذلك وجب أن يكون كل واحد من تلك الأجزاء على شكل الكرة، فوجب أن يكون بدن الإنسان على صورة شكل كرات مضمومة بعضها إلى البعض، ومعلوم أن الأمر The fourth proof for establishing the Maker is the argument from the origination of attributes. Scholars have restricted it to two types: internal signs (dala'il al-anfus) and external signs (dala'il al-afaq). As for the internal signs: it is the argument from the formation of man from the sperm-drop (nutfa). God Almighty mentioned this evidence in the Mighty Qur'an in many verses. Its exposition is that we say: the drop is a body similar in its parts in form and shape. Then either it is said that it is similar in parts in reality or it is not so. This is because the physicians say: when the heat of desire overcomes the body, a melting of all the organs occurs, some separating from the melting of bone, some from the melting of flesh, some from the melting of the eye, some from the melting of the heart. So it is, although similar in reality and form in sensation, yet different in reality. Bone is generated from what melted from bone, nerve from what melted from nerve, and on this analogy all organs. If you understand this, we say: if the drop is a body homogeneous in parts in reality, we say: there is no doubt that the effect of the heat of the moist temperament and the effect of the forces of the planets upon it are uniform. Whenever the effect of the agent is similar and the effect of the parts of the recipient in essence and nature are similar, the effect must be similar. For this reason the philosophers said: the shape of the simple is the sphere. They said: because the power of nature in the simple is one and the recipient is similar, so the shape must be a similar shape, which is the sphere. Since sense indicates that the body is composed of different organs in quantity, quality, shape, nature, and property, it is necessary to conclude that the effecting agent in its formation is not nature nor the forces of the planets, but rather a wise Maker, manager, with power and choice. As for the view of those who say: the drop, although a body similar in parts in form, yet is different in parts in nature. We say: every composite must be composed of parts each of which is simple in itself and in reality. If so, each of those parts is a recipient similar in parts in reality, and the active natural power in it is one power. When the matter is such, each of those parts must be spherical in shape, so the human body must be in the form of a shape of spheres attached to one another, and it is known that the matter is not so. Also, the drop is a thin moisture, and whatever is such does not preserve the arrangement of parts nor the proportion of some to others. Thus the part obtained from the melting of the head may become lower, and the part obtained from the melting of the heart may be higher. It ought to be that the arrangement of organs and their placement does not remain uniform in most cases. Since the matter is not so, we know that... (text incomplete).
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage introduces the fourth proof for the existence of the Maker, based on the origination of attributes (huduth al-sifat), which is divided into internal signs (dala'il al-anfus) and external signs (dala'il al-afaq). Here Razi develops the internal sign: the formation of a human from a sperm-drop. The argument proceeds in two scenarios. First, if the drop is homogeneous in reality, then the effects of natural causes (heat, planetary forces) would be uniform, producing a uniform outcome (like a sphere). But the human body is diverse in organs, so it cannot arise from nature alone; it requires a wise Maker. Second, if the drop is heterogeneous in reality but homogeneous in appearance, then its components are simple and uniform, so again natural forces would produce spherical shapes, but the body is not spherical. Moreover, the fluid nature of the drop cannot maintain order, yet the body consistently exhibits a fixed arrangement. Therefore, the formation must be by a wise, powerful Creator. The passage ends mid-sentence, implying a conclusion that we know there is a Maker.

حدوث الصفات

صانع حكيم

Correction: Razi shows that natural forces would produce uniformity or disorder, not the complex, ordered diversity of the human body, so a wise Creator is necessary.

?
Razi argues that the fluid drop cannot preserve its own order, yet your body maintains itself day after day. Where in your life are you taking that preservation for granted? Will you consciously pause today to acknowledge that every breath and heartbeat is sustained by the wise Maker, not by your own effort?
?
If natural causes alone cannot account for the intricate design of your body, then how much more does your very existence depend on Allah's constant creative act? Are you living as if you are self-sufficient, or are you ready to let this proof reshape your reliance on Him alone?

The Proof from the Homogeneous Sperm-Drop
Razi argues from the homogeneous sperm-drop to the necessity of a wise Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that if the sperm-drop were homogeneous, uniform causes would produce a uniform body, but since the body is diverse, the Creator must be a wise agent.

Core Idea
Uniform causes on a uniform drop should produce a uniform body – but our bodies are not uniform.

Razi begins his proof from the self by examining the nature of the sperm-drop. He considers two possibilities: that the drop is truly homogeneous or not. In this lesson, we follow the first scenario and see why it leads to the conclusion that the cause of the body's formation cannot be mere nature or planets.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the translation. Focus on the flow of the argument.
Notice how Razi sets up the two scenarios early on.
2
Understand the medical background
Razi cites physicians who say the sperm-drop is a mixture from melted organs. Even if it appears homogeneous, it may be heterogeneous in reality. This is key to the first scenario.
3
Follow the logical steps
If the drop is truly homogeneous, then the external causes (heat, planets) are uniform and the recipient is uniform, so the effect should be uniform. But the body is diverse, so the cause must be a wise Creator, not nature or planets.
Razi uses a philosophical principle: uniform cause + uniform recipient = uniform effect.
4
Identify the conclusion
The conclusion is that the agent is a wise Maker (صانع حكيم). Note that Razi explicitly denies nature and planetary powers as sufficient causes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما دلائل الأنفس: فهى الاستدلال بتكون الإنسان من النطفة، والله تعالى ذكر هذه الدلالة في القرآن العظيم في آيات كثيرة، وتقريرها أن نقول : النطفة جسم متشابه الأجزاء في الصورة والشكل فإما أن يقال: إنها متشابهة الأجزاء في الحقيقة أو ليست كذلك، وذلك لأن الأطباء يقولون : إن عند استيلاء حرارة الشهوة على البدن يحصل ذوبان لجملة الأعضاء، فبعضها ينفصل من ذوبان العظم وبعضها من ذوبان اللحم وبعضها من ذوبان العين وبعضها من ذوبان القلب، فهو إن كان متشابه الحقيقة والصورة في الحس إلا أنه مختلف في الحقيقة، فالعظم يتولد مما ذاب من العظم والعصب يتولد مما ذاب من العصب، وعلى هذا القياس الأعضاء. إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : إن كانت النطفة جسمًا متشابه الأجزاء في الحقيقة فنقول: لا شك أن تأثير حرارة الرخوي المزاج، وتأثير قوي الكوكب بالنسبة إليه على السوية، ومهما كان تأثير المؤثر متشابها وتأثير أجزاء القابل في الماهية والطبيعة متشابهة، وجب أن يكون الأثر متشابها، ولهذا السبب فإن الفلاسفة قالوا : شكل البسيط هو الكرة، قالوا : لأن قوة الطبيعة في البسيط واحدة والقابل متشابه فوجب أن يكون الشكل شكلا متشابهاً، وهو الكرة، ولما دل الحس على كون البدن مركبا من أعضاء مختلفة في الكمية والكيفية والشكل والطبيعة والخاصية لزم القطع بأن المؤثر في تخليقها ليس هو الطبيعة ولا قوى الكواكب، بل صانع حكيم مدبر بالقدرة والاختيار. أما على قول من يقول : النطفة وإن كانت جسما متشابه الأجزاء في الصورة لكنها مختلفة الأجزاء في الطبيعة. فنقول : إن كل مركب لا بد وأن يكون مركبًا من أجزاء كل واحد منها يكون بسيطا في نفس الأمر وفي الحقيقة، وإذا كان كذلك فكل واحد من تلك الأجزاء يكون قابلا متشابه الأجزاء في الحقيقة، وتكون للقوة الطبيعية الفاعلة فيها قوة واحدة، ومتى كان الأمر كذلك وجب أن يكون كل واحد من تلك الأجزاء على شكل الكرة، فوجب أن يكون بدن الإنسان على صورة شكل كرات مضمومة بعضها إلى البعض، ومعلوم أن الأمر ليس كذلك. وأيضًا فالنطفة رطوبة رقيقة وما كان كذلك فإنه لا يحفظ ترتيب الأجزاء ولا نسبة بعضها إلى بعض فالجزء الذي يحصل من ذوبان الرأس قد يصير أسفل، والجزء الذي يحصل من ذوبان القلب قد يكون فوق، وكان ينبغي أن لا يبقى ترتيب الأعضاء ووضعها على نسبة واحدة في الأكثر ، ولما لم يكن الأمر كذلك علمنا أن انخلاق كل واحد من هذه الأعضاء وبقاءها على ترتيبها بتخليق قادر حكيم.
As for the proofs from the self: they are the inference from the creation of man from the sperm-drop. God Almighty mentioned this proof in the Great Qur'an in many verses. Its elaboration is that we say: The sperm-drop is a body homogeneous in parts in form and shape. Then either it is said that it is homogeneous in parts in reality or not. That is because physicians say that when the heat of desire overwhelms the body, a melting of the totality of the organs occurs, and some of it separates from the melting of bone, some from the melting of flesh, some from the melting of the eye, and some from the melting of the heart. Thus, even if it is homogeneous in reality and form in sense, yet it is different in reality. So bone is generated from what melted from bone, and nerve is generated from what melted from nerve, and on this analogy are the organs. If you know this, we say: If the sperm-drop is a body homogeneous in parts in reality, then we say: There is no doubt that the effect of the heat of the moist temperament and the effect of the powers of the planets upon it are equally influenced. Whenever the effect of the agent is similar and the effect of the parts of the recipient in essence and nature are similar, then the effect must be similar. For this reason, the philosophers said: The shape of the simple [body] is the sphere. They said because the power of nature in the simple is one, and the recipient is similar, so the shape must be a similar shape, which is the sphere. Since sense indicates that the body is composed of organs different in quantity, quality, shape, nature, and property, it is necessary to decide that the agent in their creation is not nature nor the powers of the planets, but a wise Maker, a manager by power and choice. As for the view of those who say: The sperm-drop, although a body homogeneous in parts in form, yet it is different in parts in nature. We say: Every compound must be composed of parts each of which is simple in itself and in reality. If that is so, then each of those parts is a recipient homogeneous in parts in reality, and there is a single power of the active nature in it. Whenever the matter is thus, it is necessary that each of those parts be spherical in shape. Then the human body must be in the form of a shape of spheres attached to one another, and it is known that the matter is not so. Also, the sperm-drop is a thin moisture, and whatever is so does not preserve the arrangement of parts nor the proportion of some to others. So the part that results from the melting of the head may become lower, and the part that results from the melting of the heart may be higher. It would be expected that the arrangement of organs and their placement would not remain at a single proportion in most cases. Since the matter is not so, we know that the creation of each of these organs and their persistence in their arrangement is by the creation of a powerful wise [Creator].
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents a rational proof for the existence of a wise Creator based on the formation of the human body from a single drop. The proof is classified as a proof from the self (دلائل الأنفس). Razi begins by stating that this proof is mentioned in the Qur'an. The argument proceeds as follows: The sperm-drop appears homogeneous in form, but physicians say it is actually a mixture from different organs (bone, flesh, eye, heart). Two scenarios are considered. First, if the drop is truly homogeneous in reality (despite the different origins), then uniform external causes (heat, planetary influences) should produce a uniform effect. But the body is diverse, so the cause cannot be nature or planets but must be a wise, choosing agent. Second, if the drop is heterogeneous in nature, then each simple component should be spherical (like a simple body), but the body is not a sphere. Also, the watery nature of the drop would not maintain order. Therefore, the order and diversity of organs prove they were created by a powerful, wise Creator. The proof refutes naturalistic and astrological explanations.

Key Terms
دلائل الأنفس
النطفة
قوى الكواكب
صانع حكيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion Razi draws from the first scenario (homogeneous drop)?
A) The body is created by nature
B) The body is created by planetary forces
C) The body is created by a wise Maker
D) The body is the result of chance

Key Takeaway
The diversity of the human body proves that its creator is not nature or planets but a wise, choosing God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the diversity of your own body—your hands, eyes, heart—do you ever pause to see it as a sign pointing beyond nature? What keeps you from living in constant awareness that you are fashioned by a wise Maker, not chance?
?
If this argument is true, then your very existence demands a response to your Creator. Have you been living as if your body is a product of random forces, or are you actively acknowledging the One who shaped you with purpose? What will you change today to honor that?
?
The philosophers claimed a uniform cause yields a uniform effect, but your body defies that. Are there areas of your life where you expect uniformity—where you resist the diversity and complexity God has placed in you? How can you trust the wisdom of your Maker in those areas instead of insisting on your own simple explanations?

The Proof from the Heterogeneous Sperm-Drop
Razi refutes naturalistic explanations by arguing that a heterogeneous drop fails to explain the body's non-spherical shape and maintained order.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's second scenario: if the drop is heterogeneous, each simple part should be spherical, and the watery nature should disrupt order – but the body remains ordered, proving a wise Creator.

Core Idea
A heterogeneous drop should produce a spherical body or chaos – but we see neither.

Razi now considers the view that the sperm-drop is heterogeneous in nature, having components from different organs. He provides two further arguments against naturalistic explanations: first, each simple component should be spherical, but the body is not spherical; second, the watery nature of the drop would not preserve order, yet the body has consistent organ arrangement. Both point to a wise Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage for the second scenario and its translation. Notice the two distinct arguments.
2
Understand the first argument (sphere)
If the drop is heterogeneous, each simple part should be spherical (like simple bodies). The human body would then be a collection of spheres, but it is not. So the cause cannot be nature.
This is a philosophical argument based on the nature of simples.
3
Understand the second argument (order)
The sperm-drop is a thin moisture, which cannot preserve the arrangement of parts. Yet organs maintain their relative positions. This indicates a powerful, wise agent.
This argument focuses on the vulnerability of watery mixtures to displacement.
4
Compare both scenarios
Notice that whether the drop is homogeneous or heterogeneous, the conclusion is the same: only a wise Creator can explain the body's formation.
Razi uses exhaustive reasoning (division into two possibilities).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما دلائل الأنفس: فهى الاستدلال بتكون الإنسان من النطفة، والله تعالى ذكر هذه الدلالة في القرآن العظيم في آيات كثيرة، وتقريرها أن نقول : النطفة جسم متشابه الأجزاء في الصورة والشكل فإما أن يقال: إنها متشابهة الأجزاء في الحقيقة أو ليست كذلك، وذلك لأن الأطباء يقولون : إن عند استيلاء حرارة الشهوة على البدن يحصل ذوبان لجملة الأعضاء، فبعضها ينفصل من ذوبان العظم وبعضها من ذوبان اللحم وبعضها من ذوبان العين وبعضها من ذوبان القلب، فهو إن كان متشابه الحقيقة والصورة في الحس إلا أنه مختلف في الحقيقة، فالعظم يتولد مما ذاب من العظم والعصب يتولد مما ذاب من العصب، وعلى هذا القياس الأعضاء. إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : إن كانت النطفة جسمًا متشابه الأجزاء في الحقيقة فنقول: لا شك أن تأثير حرارة الرخوي المزاج، وتأثير قوي الكوكب بالنسبة إليه على السوية، ومهما كان تأثير المؤثر متشابها وتأثير أجزاء القابل في الماهية والطبيعة متشابهة، وجب أن يكون الأثر متشابها، ولهذا السبب فإن الفلاسفة قالوا : شكل البسيط هو الكرة، قالوا : لأن قوة الطبيعة في البسيط واحدة والقابل متشابه فوجب أن يكون الشكل شكلا متشابهاً، وهو الكرة، ولما دل الحس على كون البدن مركبا من أعضاء مختلفة في الكمية والكيفية والشكل والطبيعة والخاصية لزم القطع بأن المؤثر في تخليقها ليس هو الطبيعة ولا قوى الكواكب، بل صانع حكيم مدبر بالقدرة والاختيار. أما على قول من يقول : النطفة وإن كانت جسما متشابه الأجزاء في الصورة لكنها مختلفة الأجزاء في الطبيعة. فنقول : إن كل مركب لا بد وأن يكون مركبًا من أجزاء كل واحد منها يكون بسيطا في نفس الأمر وفي الحقيقة، وإذا كان كذلك فكل واحد من تلك الأجزاء يكون قابلا متشابه الأجزاء في الحقيقة، وتكون للقوة الطبيعية الفاعلة فيها قوة واحدة، ومتى كان الأمر كذلك وجب أن يكون كل واحد من تلك الأجزاء على شكل الكرة، فوجب أن يكون بدن الإنسان على صورة شكل كرات مضمومة بعضها إلى البعض، ومعلوم أن الأمر ليس كذلك. وأيضًا فالنطفة رطوبة رقيقة وما كان كذلك فإنه لا يحفظ ترتيب الأجزاء ولا نسبة بعضها إلى بعض فالجزء الذي يحصل من ذوبان الرأس قد يصير أسفل، والجزء الذي يحصل من ذوبان القلب قد يكون فوق، وكان ينبغي أن لا يبقى ترتيب الأعضاء ووضعها على نسبة واحدة في الأكثر ، ولما لم يكن الأمر كذلك علمنا أن انخلاق كل واحد من هذه الأعضاء وبقاءها على ترتيبها بتخليق قادر حكيم.
As for the proofs from the self: they are the inference from the creation of man from the sperm-drop. God Almighty mentioned this proof in the Great Qur'an in many verses. Its elaboration is that we say: The sperm-drop is a body homogeneous in parts in form and shape. Then either it is said that it is homogeneous in parts in reality or not. That is because physicians say that when the heat of desire overwhelms the body, a melting of the totality of the organs occurs, and some of it separates from the melting of bone, some from the melting of flesh, some from the melting of the eye, and some from the melting of the heart. Thus, even if it is homogeneous in reality and form in sense, yet it is different in reality. So bone is generated from what melted from bone, and nerve is generated from what melted from nerve, and on this analogy are the organs. If you know this, we say: If the sperm-drop is a body homogeneous in parts in reality, then we say: There is no doubt that the effect of the heat of the moist temperament and the effect of the powers of the planets upon it are equally influenced. Whenever the effect of the agent is similar and the effect of the parts of the recipient in essence and nature are similar, then the effect must be similar. For this reason, the philosophers said: The shape of the simple [body] is the sphere. They said because the power of nature in the simple is one, and the recipient is similar, so the shape must be a similar shape, which is the sphere. Since sense indicates that the body is composed of organs different in quantity, quality, shape, nature, and property, it is necessary to decide that the agent in their creation is not nature nor the powers of the planets, but a wise Maker, a manager by power and choice. As for the view of those who say: The sperm-drop, although a body homogeneous in parts in form, yet it is different in parts in nature. We say: Every compound must be composed of parts each of which is simple in itself and in reality. If that is so, then each of those parts is a recipient homogeneous in parts in reality, and there is a single power of the active nature in it. Whenever the matter is thus, it is necessary that each of those parts be spherical in shape. Then the human body must be in the form of a shape of spheres attached to one another, and it is known that the matter is not so. Also, the sperm-drop is a thin moisture, and whatever is so does not preserve the arrangement of parts nor the proportion of some to others. So the part that results from the melting of the head may become lower, and the part that results from the melting of the heart may be higher. It would be expected that the arrangement of organs and their placement would not remain at a single proportion in most cases. Since the matter is not so, we know that the creation of each of these organs and their persistence in their arrangement is by the creation of a powerful wise [Creator].
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents a rational proof for the existence of a wise Creator based on the formation of the human body from a single drop. The proof is classified as a proof from the self (دلائل الأنفس). Razi begins by stating that this proof is mentioned in the Qur'an. The argument proceeds as follows: The sperm-drop appears homogeneous in form, but physicians say it is actually a mixture from different organs (bone, flesh, eye, heart). Two scenarios are considered. First, if the drop is truly homogeneous in reality (despite the different origins), then uniform external causes (heat, planetary influences) should produce a uniform effect. But the body is diverse, so the cause cannot be nature or planets but must be a wise, choosing agent. Second, if the drop is heterogeneous in nature, then each simple component should be spherical (like a simple body), but the body is not a sphere. Also, the watery nature of the drop would not maintain order. Therefore, the order and diversity of organs prove they were created by a powerful, wise Creator. The proof refutes naturalistic and astrological explanations.

Key Terms
النطفة
قوى الكواكب
صانع حكيم
بسيط

Checkpoint
According to Razi, what would happen if the sperm-drop were heterogeneous in nature?
A) The body would be a sphere
B) The body would be a cluster of spheres
C) The body would be irregular and chaotic
D) The body would be the same as now

Key Takeaway
Even if the drop is not uniform, natural processes cannot account for the body's design – a wise Creator is necessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your body's very shape testifies against random chance, how does that challenge the way you look at yourself in the mirror each day? Will you acknowledge the Creator's hand in your form, not just in your faith?
?
Razi argues that a thin moisture cannot hold order—yet your organs are perfectly placed. When was the last time you thanked the One who maintains that arrangement, moment by moment, without you even noticing?
?
You accept that your body is designed; but do you live as if it belongs to its Designer? What would change today if you truly believed that every bone and vessel is a deliberate sign from a powerful, wise Creator?

Answering the Objection of Alternative Creators
Razi raises an objection and answers by referring to previous proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi handles an objection by referring to prior established proofs, and why this method is valid in theological argumentation.

Core Idea
Previous proofs are the foundation for answering new objections.

In the previous lesson, Razi presented a proof from the creation of the human body. Now he anticipates a possible objection: why not attribute creation to angels or planets? This lesson shows how he answers by pointing back to earlier arguments, reinforcing the cumulative nature of theological proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once. Note that Razi introduces the objection with 'إلا أنه بقي مهنا أن يقال' meaning 'except that there remains to be said'.
2
Understand the basis of the objection
The objection suggests that angels or planets could be the creators because they are 'living, rational, active, choosing'. Consider why this seems plausible if one hasn't already accepted the earlier proofs.
Razi doesn't elaborate on these terms; they are common attributes of agents.
3
Notice the answer and its method
The answer is simply 'وعند ذلك لا بد من الرجوع إلى البراهين المتقدمة' — one must return to the preceding proofs. Reflect on why this is a valid response: because the earlier arguments already established that only Allah is the Creator.
This shows the cumulative structure of kalam: earlier conclusions are used to answer later objections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا أنه بقي مهنا أن يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال: إنما حصلت بتخليق بعض الملائكة أو بتخليق الكواكب، فإنها أحياء ناطقة فاعلة مختارة؟ وعند ذلك لا بد من الرجوع إلى البراهين المتقدمة.
Except that there remains here to be said: Why may it not be said that these [organs] came about by the creation of some angels or by the creation of the planets, for they are living, rational, active, choosing [beings]? And upon that, one must return to the preceding proofs.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is an objection and its answer. After presenting the proof from the creation of the human body, Razi anticipates a possible objection: why not attribute the creation to angels or planets, since they are living, rational, and have free will? The answer is brief: one must refer back to earlier proofs (البراهين المتقدمة). These earlier proofs, presumably from earlier sections of the book (though not included here), establish that only God is the Creator and that angels and planets are created and cannot be independent creators. The objection is thus dismissed by an appeal to prior arguments.

Key Terms
ملائكة
كواكب
براهين متقدمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the objection Razi considers regarding the creation of the human body?
A) That the body could be created by chance
B) That the body could be created by some angels or planets
C) That the body could be eternal
D) That the body could be created by humans

Key Takeaway
Razi answers the objection by reminding the reader of the conclusions of earlier proofs, showing the cumulative structure of kalam argumentation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When a subtle doubt about Allah's exclusive creative power crosses your mind, do you quickly turn to the clear proofs that have already settled the matter, or do you allow the doubt to linger and unsettle your faith? What specific proof will you memorize and recall next time?
?
Consider a blessing in your life—your health, a skill, a relationship. Do you habitually attribute it to secondary causes (your effort, another person, chance) instead of immediately recognizing Allah as its sole Creator? How can you train your heart to see His hand first?
?
If the intricate design of your own body does not compel you to awe of its Maker, what will? Set a time today to reflect on one of your organs, trace its function, and say: 'Only Allah could have created this.' Will you do it?

Two Kinds of External Proofs: Elemental and Celestial
Razi categorizes external proofs into lower elemental and higher celestial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's two-fold classification of external proofs (دلائل الآفاق) into lower elemental and higher celestial categories, and how both serve as signs pointing to the Creator.

Core Idea
Razi divides external signs into those from the lower world and those from the heavens.

This passage presents Razi's systematic categorization of the external signs (آفاق) that point to the Creator. He distinguishes between signs from the elemental realm—including animals, plants, minerals, and atmospheric phenomena—and signs from the celestial realm of spheres and planets. Understanding this classification helps us appreciate the Qur'anic methodology of drawing proofs from the created world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the clear division into two types.
The passage is short but packed with meaning.
2
Identify the two categories
Find the two categories: lower elemental (سفلية عنصرية) and higher celestial (علوية فلكية). Note the examples given for each.
The examples for lower include animals, plants, minerals, and atmospheric phenomena.
3
Connect to the Qur'an and Razi's work
Razi says the exhaustive treatment is in the Qur'an and in his own book 'Asrar al-Tanzil'. Reflect on how this shows the Qur'anic origin of such proofs.
4
Test your understanding
Try the checkpoint question to ensure you can distinguish between the two categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما دلائل الآفاق فبعضها سفلية عنصرية، ومجامعها الاستدلال بأحوال الحيوان والنبات والمعادن والآثار العلوية وبعضها علوية فلكية، ومجامعها الاستدلال بأحوال الأفلاك والكواكب . والاستقصاء في هذا النوع من الدلائل مذكور في القرآن العظيم ومشروح في كتابنا المسمى بأسرار التنزيل وأنوار التأويل.
As for the proofs of the horizons, some of them are lower elemental, and their sums are the inference from the states of animals, plants, minerals, and upper atmospheric phenomena; and some of them are higher celestial, and their sums are the inference from the states of the spheres and planets. The exhaustive treatment of this type of proofs is mentioned in the Great Qur'an and explained in our book titled 'Asrar al-Tanzil wa-Anwar al-Ta'wil'.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the second broad category of proofs for God's existence: the proofs of the horizons (دلائل الآفاق). Razi divides them into two types: lower elemental (سفلية عنصرية) which involve inference from the conditions of animals, plants, minerals, and atmospheric phenomena; and higher celestial (علوية فلكية) which involve inference from the states of the heavens (spheres) and planets. Razi notes that a comprehensive treatment of this type of proofs is found in the Qur'an and in his own book 'Asrar al-Tanzil wa-Anwar al-Ta'wil' (Secrets of Revelation and Lights of Interpretation). This classification provides a systematic framework for the external signs that point to the Creator.

Key Terms
دلائل الآفاق
سفلية عنصرية
علوية فلكية
أسرار التنزيل وأنوار التأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking 'آثار علوية' in the lower category refers to celestial beings or the heavens.
Correction: Razi uses 'آثار علوية' to mean atmospheric phenomena (like rain, clouds, etc.), not celestial objects. The lower category deals with the sub-lunar world, while the celestial category deals with the spheres and planets.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, what does the lower elemental category (سفلية عنصرية) include?
A) The states of spheres and planets
B) The states of animals, plants, minerals, and atmospheric phenomena
C) The states of angels and jinn
D) The states of the intellect and soul

Key Takeaway
Razi divides the proofs from the horizons into two types: lower elemental (involving animals, plants, minerals, atmospheric phenomena) and higher celestial (involving spheres and planets), both of which are detailed in the Qur'an and his own commentary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe an animal, a plant, or the weather today, do you pause to see it as a proof pointing to the Creator? Reflect on a specific recent experience where you missed this sign. What will you do tomorrow to be more mindful of these lower elemental proofs?
?
Razi mentions that the exhaustive treatment of these proofs is in the Qur'an. How often do you read the Qur'an with the intention of finding these signs? What is one verse you can study this week to deepen your understanding of the celestial proofs?
?
Which category of proofs—lower elemental or higher celestial—do you find easier to ignore in your daily life? Why? Make a concrete plan to intentionally observe the neglected category before the end of this week.

God's Eternity and the Objection from Intermediaries
Razi presents the argument for God's eternity and the first objection from intermediaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classical theological argument for God's eternity based on avoiding infinite regress and the first objection from those who posit intermediaries.

Core Idea
God's eternity is proven by the impossibility of infinite regress, but intermediaries pose a challenge.

This lesson presents the Fourth Issue from Razi's al-Arba'in, where he discusses God's eternity. After establishing the Necessary Existent, Razi notes that earlier theologians used a different argument: if the Maker of the world were originated, it would require another originator, leading to infinite regress. However, an objection arises: perhaps the world's immediate creator is originated, created by an eternal being. This is the view of those who posit intermediaries. We will examine this argument and objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the flow from the argument to the objection.
The passage cuts off mid-second objection; focus on the first objection.
2
Identify the argument for eternity
Find the premise: if the Maker were originated, it would need another originator, leading to infinite regress, which is impossible. Therefore the Maker is eternal.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Understand the first objection
The objector suggests that the creator of this world could be originated, but its creator is eternal. This would avoid infinite regress while allowing the world's immediate cause to be originated.
This is the view of the Mufawwida and philosophers who posit a chain of intellects.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this objection matters: it challenges the direct inference from the world's contingency to God's eternity. Without a refutation, the argument for God's eternity is incomplete.
Razi would go on to refute this, but the passage ends before that.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الرابعة في أن الله تعالى قديم أزلي أبدي سرمدي. اعلم أنا لما دللنا في المسألة الثالثة على وجوب انتهاء الممكنات إلى موجود واجب الوجود لذاته وكل ما كان واجب الوجود لذاته فإن حقيقته لا تقبل العدم أصلا، وكل ما كان كذلك فإنه يجب أن يكون قديما أزليا باقيا أبديًا، فعلى هذا لا نحتاج بعد ذلك إلى إقامة الدلالة على كونه تعالى أبديًا إلا أن المتكلمين الذين كانوا قبلنا لما لم يذكروا تلك الطريقة في إثبات واجب الوجود لا جرم كانوا معولين في إثبات كونه تعالى أزليّا أبديًا على وجوه أخر، فنحن أردنا أن نتبرك بإيراد تلك الوجوه أيضا. واعلم أن مشايخ المتكلمين لما أقاموا الدلالة على افتقار العالم إلى صانع قالوا: صانع العالم لو كان محدثًا لافتقر إلى محدث آخر، ولزم التسلسل، وهو محال، فوجب القول بأن صانع العالم قديم. فإن قيل : الإشكال على هذا الاستدلال من وجوه : الأول: لِمَ لا يجوز أن يقال : خالق هذا العالم المحسوس شيء محدث، وخالق ذلك المحدث شيء قديم، وعلى هذا التقدير يكون صانع العالم محدثًا ولا يلزم التسلسل أيضاً، وهذا هو قول المفوضة وأصحاب الوسائط، ألا ترى أن الفلاسفة يقولون : مدبر ما تحت كرة القمر هو العقل، وهذا العقل الفعال معلول عقل آخر، وذلك العقل معلول عقل آخر إلى عشر مراتب وأكثر، ثم ذلك العقل الأول معلول وجود الله تعالى، وعند المفوضة: الإله الأكبر خلق السيارات السبع، وفوض تدبير هذا العالم إليها، وإذا كان هذا الاحتمال قائمًا فلا بد من إبطاله. السؤال الثاني: أن كل موجودين يُفْرَضَان فلا بد وأن يكونا إما معا أو يكون أحدهما سابقًا على الآخر، فإن كانا معًا لزم أن يكونا قديمين أو محدثين، لكنكم
The Fourth Issue: That God Almighty is eternal, pre-eternal, everlasting, perpetual. Know that when we demonstrated in the Third Issue the necessity of contingent things terminating at an existent necessary of existence in itself, and everything that is necessary of existence in itself, its essence admits not non-existence at all, and everything that is like that must be eternal, pre-eternal, remaining, everlasting. Thus, after that we do not need to establish evidence for His being everlasting, except that the theologians who were before us, since they did not mention that method in proving the Necessary Existent, they inevitably relied in proving His being pre-eternal and everlasting on other methods. So we wanted to seek blessing by presenting those methods as well. Know that the leading theologians, when they established evidence for the world's need of a Maker, said: If the Maker of the world were originated, it would need another originator, and infinite regress would follow, which is impossible. So it is necessary to say that the Maker of the world is eternal. If it is said: The objection to this argument is from several aspects: The first: Why is it not permissible to say: The creator of this sensible world is an originated thing, and the creator of that originated thing is an eternal thing? On this assumption, the Maker of the world would be originated and infinite regress would not follow either. This is the saying of the Mufawwida and the proponents of intermediaries. Do you not see that the philosophers say: The manager of what is under the sphere of the moon is the intellect, and this active intellect is an effect of another intellect, and that intellect is an effect of another intellect up to ten levels or more, then that first intellect is an effect of the existence of God. And according to the Mufawwida: The greatest god created the seven planets and delegated the management of this world to them. Since this possibility stands, it must be refuted. The second question: Any two existents that are assumed must either be simultaneous or one precedes the other. If they are simultaneous, it follows that they are both eternal or both originated, but you...
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the Fourth Issue concerning God's eternity. Razi first notes that from the proof of the Necessary Existent in the Third Issue, it follows directly that God is eternal without need for further proof. However, earlier theologians did not use that method, so they relied on other arguments. Razi then presents the classical argument from contingency: if the Maker of the world were originated, He would require another originator, leading to an infinite regress, which is impossible, so the Maker must be eternal. Then an objection is raised: why not say that the creator of this world is originated, but that originated being was created by an eternal being? This would avoid infinite regress. This is the view of the Mufawwida (those who delegate creation to intermediaries) and the philosophers who posit a chain of intellects. Razi then starts to mention a second objection regarding the simultaneity of two existents, but the text cuts off. The passage thus sets up the objection that needs to be refuted.

Key Terms
قديم
أزلي
أبدي
سرمدي
واجب الوجود
المفوضة
أصحاب الوسائط
التسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection claims that God Himself could be originated.
Correction: The objection does not say God is originated; it says the world's immediate creator could be originated, while God (its creator) is eternal.

Checkpoint
What is the main argument presented by the earlier theologians for God's eternity according to Razi?
A) The world is created, so its creator must be eternal.
B) If the Maker were originated, infinite regress would result.
C) The Quran says God is eternal.
D) The philosophers proved it.

Key Takeaway
The classical argument for God's eternity relies on the impossibility of infinite regress, but the objection from intermediaries challenges this by positing a chain of created causes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage reveals that some people, like the Mufawwida, attempted to distance God from direct creation by inserting intermediaries. Where in your own life do you avoid attributing events directly to God, preferring indirect explanations? What would change if you truly believed He is the immediate cause of everything?
?
The argument for God's eternity hinges on the impossibility of infinite regress. Consider: Are there endless cycles in your own thinking—like always seeking worldly causes for your happiness instead of anchoring it in the Eternal? How would your daily decisions shift if you truly stopped that regression and rested in God as your ultimate cause?
?
Razi notes that earlier theologians did not use the proof of the Necessary Existent, relying instead on other arguments. Do you sometimes lean on secondary proofs for your faith rather than the direct certainty of God's necessary existence? What step can you take this week to move from borrowed arguments to a personal, unshakable conviction of His eternity?

Allah's Existence
